  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cf330aae-5458-4307-b855-f86d33247d68'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3935710545839050879">Audere, agere, auferre. To dare, to strive, to conquer. For generations, privileged young men have attended St. Oswald's Grammar School for Boys, groomed for success by the likes of Roy Straitley, the eccentric Classics teacher who has been a fixture there for more than thirty years. But this year the wind of unwelcome change is blowing. Suits, paperwork, and information t</span>
  <span id="freeText3935710545839050879" style="display:none">Audere, agere, auferre. To dare, to strive, to conquer. For generations, privileged young men have attended St. Oswald's Grammar School for Boys, groomed for success by the likes of Roy Straitley, the eccentric Classics teacher who has been a fixture there for more than thirty years. But this year the wind of unwelcome change is blowing. Suits, paperwork, and information technology are beginning to overshadow St. Oswald's tradition, and Straitley is finally, and reluctantly, contemplating retirement. He is joined this term by five new faculty members, including one who -- unbeknownst to Straitley and everyone else -- holds intimate and dangerous knowledge of St. Oswald's ways and secrets. Harboring dark ties to the school's past, this young teacher has arrived with one terrible goal: to destroy St. Oswald's.<br /><br />As the new term gets under way, a number of incidents befall students and faculty alike. Beginning as small annoyances -- a lost pen, a misplaced coffee mug -- they are initially overlooked. But as the incidents escalate in both number and consequence, it soon becomes apparent that a darker undercurrent is stirring within the school. With St. Oswald's unraveling, only Straitley stands in the way of its ruin. The veteran teacher faces a formidable opponent, however -- a master player with a bitter grudge and a strategy that has been meticulously planned to the final move, a secret game with very real, very deadly consequences.<br /><br />A harrowing tale of cat and mouse, this riveting, hypnotically atmospheric novel showcases <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Joanne Harris's astonishing storytelling talent as never before.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3935710545839050879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_146034').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_146034').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_146034').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1009330-i-loved-this-book-in-fact-i-love-all-of">I loved this book. In fact, I love all of Joanne Harris&#39;s books, and it&#39;s a tossup to say which one is best. One thing I AM confused about though, why is Straitley&#39;s group of favorite boys called &quot;Brodie Boys&quot;? I even googled this but came up with nothing to explain why this name would be a thing. Does anyone know?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1009330'><a id="like_count_community_question_1009330" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1009330?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F15102.Gentlemen_and_Players">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2242287-kay"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2242287-kay">Kay</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
It's a reference to Muriel Spark's "The Prime of Miss Jean Brodie" where the teacher, Miss Brodie, has her own set of favourite girls. 
</span>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Sallie, I found that following the chess pieces helped to signify the narrator. There was a white king piece at the beginning of Straitley's chapte<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Sallie, I found that following the chess pieces helped to signify the narrator. There was a white king piece at the beginning of Straitley's chapters and black pawns at the beginning of the unknown narrator’s parts (at least in my copy). <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_34875740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34875740" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34875740?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34875740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10326699028880516001">St. Oswalds Grammar School for Boys is an exclusive British institution, a bastion of tradition and privilege. Roy Straitley is an aging Classics teacher about to reach his 100th term at the school. The sameness and relative serenity of St Oswalds is about to be shattered. A new teacher is up to no good, determined to wreak havoc, perhaps even destroy the school and all those in it. Ultimately, this will become a battle between the honorable Straitley and the wretch bent on revenge and destructi</span>
  <span id="freeText10326699028880516001" style="display:none">St. Oswalds Grammar School for Boys is an exclusive British institution, a bastion of tradition and privilege. Roy Straitley is an aging Classics teacher about to reach his 100th term at the school. The sameness and relative serenity of St Oswalds is about to be shattered. A new teacher is up to no good, determined to wreak havoc, perhaps even destroy the school and all those in it. Ultimately, this will become a battle between the honorable Straitley and the wretch bent on revenge and destruction. This is a very engaging read, told alternately from the perspectives of Straitley and his nemesis. It takes place in two times as well, the present, in which small things disappear, evidence appears to incriminate people who are accused of crimes they did not commit. Pawns are used and sacrificed in the deadly game. We are also shown the roots of this evil, fifteen years prior, in which the young person comes to despise the school and its inhabitants. A game of chess, both then and now. Fun, fast reading, thrilling and with an excellent final-chapter twist. Heartily recommended. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10326699028880516001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_601604124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601604124" />
    <a title="B the BookAddict" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19832827-b-the-bookaddict"><img alt="B the BookAddict" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478463572p2/19832827.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601604124?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B the BookAddict" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B the BookAddict" href="/user/show/19832827-b-the-bookaddict">B the BookAddict</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Most Highly Recommended</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19832827-b-the-bookaddict?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601604124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4274734365460833311"><br/><br/><br/>Joanne Harris is best known for her award winning novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47401.Chocolat__Chocolat___1_' title='Chocolat (Chocolat, #1) by Joanne Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chocolat</a> that lead to the highly successful film of the same name and two more novels featuring the main characters. Her other novels include <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15101.Blackberry_Wine' title='Blackberry Wine by Joanne Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blackberry Wine</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15096.Five_Quarters_of_the_Orange' title='Five Quarters of the Orange by Joanne Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Five Quarters of the Orange</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1022699.The_Lollipop_Shoes' title='The Lollipop Shoes by Joanne Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lollipop Shoes</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13588138.Peaches_for_Father_Francis__Chocolat___3_' title='Peaches for Father Francis (Chocolat, #3) by Joanne Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Peaches for Father Francis</a>. Born in her grandparent’s sweet shop, her family has a tradition of storytelling, folklore, cookery and strong women. It is no surprise then that many of her books feature food, sweets and strong women fol</span>
  <span id="freeText4274734365460833311" style="display:none"><br /><br /><br />Joanne Harris is best known for her award winning novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47401.Chocolat__Chocolat___1_" title="Chocolat (Chocolat, #1) by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Chocolat</a> that lead to the highly successful film of the same name and two more novels featuring the main characters. Her other novels include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15101.Blackberry_Wine" title="Blackberry Wine by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Blackberry Wine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15096.Five_Quarters_of_the_Orange" title="Five Quarters of the Orange by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Five Quarters of the Orange</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1022699.The_Lollipop_Shoes" title="The Lollipop Shoes by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lollipop Shoes</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13588138.Peaches_for_Father_Francis__Chocolat___3_" title="Peaches for Father Francis (Chocolat, #3) by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Peaches for Father Francis</a>. Born in her grandparent’s sweet shop, her family has a tradition of storytelling, folklore, cookery and strong women. It is no surprise then that many of her books feature food, sweets and strong women following their own path. But in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15102.Gentlemen_and_Players" title="Gentlemen and Players by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Gentlemen and Players</a>, Harris changes tack completely. She has taught modern languages at a boys independent grammar school for fifteen years and from this experience, she has gleaned inspiration.<br /><br />Art does often imitate life so it should come as no surprise then that Harris has set her 2005 novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15102.Gentlemen_and_Players" title="Gentlemen and Players by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Gentlemen and Players</a> in the rarefied air of a private grammar school for boys, St Oswalds. The novel is a psychological thriller, which sharply features deceits, flawed childhood, hidden identity, class distinction and revenge; the story ends with a deliciously unexpected twist at the end. There are two narrators; Roy Straitley, the Classics Master, on the eve of his century (100th) term who is affectionately referred to, by his students, as <i>Quasi</i> or <i>Quasimodo</i> as he is a trifle hunched and whose rooms are in the Bell Tower. Straitley is a Luddite; ignoring all requests to attend to his email, he swears in Latin and smokes (banned by the school) secret Gauloises in his office. The other narrator is the unnamed perpetrator who is bent on revenge for a myriad of both real and imagined slights against St Oswalds; a sociopath who is filled with hatred and bitterness. This perpetrator knows no rules he will not break; somehow he has infiltrated the teachers ranks, become on of them; a serpent set loose in the garden. One by one, insurrection among the boys, then scandals involving the staff begin to erupt, bringing chaos to the Michaelmas term.<br /><br />A white King marks the first narrator, Straitley, at the beginning of alternate chapters. The second narrator is marked by a Black Pawn, and is the voice of the unknown enemy within St Oswald's.<br /><br /><i>“If there’s one thing I’ve learned in the past fifteen years, it’s this: murder is really no big deal.”</i><br /><br />Such a tantalising first sentence in a novel! Harris did not disappoint in the rest of the story. It is gripping, clever and well paced; the plot is tightly controlled with impressive ingenuity. A tale for <u>every</u> reader: Most Highly Recommended. 4.5★<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4274734365460833311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5333605740297059615">This book is an absolute delight from start to finish. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9432.Joanne_Harris' title='Joanne Harris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Joanne Harris</a> has always been a favourite of mine and she certainly did not let me down with this one! Mr Straitly is such a well drawn character I found myself cheering for him the whole time and I was desperate for him to succeed in the end. The last paragraphs of the book brought tears to my eyes. There is a very big mystery angle to this story and although I was able to guess the identity of the murderer fairly early on it was only becau</span>
  <span id="freeText5333605740297059615" style="display:none">This book is an absolute delight from start to finish. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9432.Joanne_Harris" title="Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Joanne Harris</a> has always been a favourite of mine and she certainly did not let me down with this one! Mr Straitly is such a well drawn character I found myself cheering for him the whole time and I was desperate for him to succeed in the end. The last paragraphs of the book brought tears to my eyes. There is a very big mystery angle to this story and although I was able to guess the identity of the murderer fairly early on it was only because having read this author before I was aware of her devious mind and looked outside the square! It was very cleverly written and very entertaining. So so good - easily five stars.</span>

    <div class="updateActionLinks">

<div id="review_1552782974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1552782974" />
    <a title="Vonia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5204784-vonia"><img alt="Vonia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584439676p2/5204784.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1552782974?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vonia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vonia" href="/user/show/5204784-vonia">Vonia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060559151" href="/book/show/15108.Gentlemen_and_Players">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=young-death">young-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=told-in-flashbacks">told-in-flashbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=death-grieving">death-grieving</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=abnormal-psychology">abnormal-psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=experimentally-creative">experimentally-creative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=unique-chapter-titles">unique-chapter-titles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=revenge">revenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1552782974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13609157840783356423">This is definitely the best book I have read so far this year. Why? Let me count the ways. Where to begin? (The only real complaint I have is that the synopsis and teasers given tell a story nothing like what readers have. At least, it reveals only a sliver, and not even a very significant one- comparatively minor enough that it changes the overall perception.) <br/><br/>1. As always, Joanne Harris is an expert at characterization. This is my 4th book by her I read and even if I did not like the book too </span>
  <span id="freeText13609157840783356423" style="display:none">This is definitely the best book I have read so far this year. Why? Let me count the ways. Where to begin? (The only real complaint I have is that the synopsis and teasers given tell a story nothing like what readers have. At least, it reveals only a sliver, and not even a very significant one- comparatively minor enough that it changes the overall perception.) <br /><br />1. As always, Joanne Harris is an expert at characterization. This is my 4th book by her I read and even if I did not like the book too much overall, her characters have consistently been relatable to the point that I was able to see them in front of me, the two-dimensional dimensional characters becoming three-dimensional. In this book, it is John Snyde, a psychopathic man, and Roy Straightly, a dedicated and loyal Classics teacher for thirty plus years. Entering the minds of these vastly different men is nothing short of fascinating. <br /><br />2. The book is set up in a chess game format. Book parts, rather than numerical, are labeled: Pawn, King, Knight, En Passant, Check, Bishop, Queen, and Mate. Readers should be told that the two points of view are differentiated by the color of the cheers piece. As for myself, without this information, I failed to notice this and was slightly confused throughout until the very last chapter, although it became pretty clear after several sentences. <br /><br />3. A psychological thriller. The thrill of the chase. A mystery. A suspenseful battle. A masterfully written all night page turner.<br /><br />4. Themes I appreciate: the shame of the LGBT community, the difficulties inherent in teaching, friendships, parenting, abnormal psychology, loyalty, and institutions and traditions ineradicable and with a character of its own. <br /><br />5. Sentimental and touching at the same time as appalling and frustrating. The ending is similar to that in Robin William's "Dead Poet's Society" (May he Rest In Peace) and quite heart warming. <br /><br />Well, unlike many mysteries and psychological thriller I have read, the eventual reveal was actually unexpected and not, like most, anticlimactic. <br /><br />**** Spoilers **** <br /><br />John Snyde is a man (and woman, as the reader find out as the story continues. He dresses up, first as a teenager posing as his "mother" Julia Snyde, then more than a decade later as a professor by the name of Diane Dare) that is driven to madness, by both his feelings of inferiority, his need for revenge, and the death of the only guy he ever really loved. As a child, because of his place on the lower end of the socioeconomic tier of life, he is excluded from the exclusive, sometimes pretentious St. Oswald's Grammar School for Boys. Because of his obsession with what he feels ruined his life, his new obsession is seeking revenge. His definition of this revenge is master planned, with a series of events and planned schemes, from spreading rumors that cause the staff to hate each other, claims of sexual abuse that tears then apart, encouragement to specifically targeted boys to rebel, missing items resulting in planted evidence, etcetera. <br /><br />His most intelligent rival can be found in Roy Straightly, whom is the one to eventually figure out his true identity and in clued in enough to unveil the truth, his true motive: he was the one (with an intense jealously of his girlfriend), many years ago, to push his (unrequited) love from the roof to his death. <br /><br />A satisfying conclusion, although far from perfect. And this is something I also really appreciate. Almost always, on happy endings are exactly that and very frustrating. On the other hand, happy endings are also frustrating in that this is nothing like real life. Here, the bad guy is not caught, having recalled to another country. But in his own way, his pain has caused him to pay for many years. Although many characters are murdered, St. Oswald's endures, as do most of the more likeable characters. <br /><br />Joanne Harris, I liked you before, but now I love you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13609157840783356423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer1082124983994606700">Delightful, engaging and well written thriller, with an interesting plot and credible characters. <br/><br/>It beautifully recreates the special atmosphere of an old, privileged, traditional educational institution, and the particular set of idiosyncrasies, values, ineradicable and peculiar attitudes that characterize teachers (as well as students) in such a unique environment. The main character, old-school teacher Straitley, is just lovely and his passion for teaching and culture are contagious. You can</span>
  <span id="freeText1082124983994606700" style="display:none">Delightful, engaging and well written thriller, with an interesting plot and credible characters. <br /><br />It beautifully recreates the special atmosphere of an old, privileged, traditional educational institution, and the particular set of idiosyncrasies, values, ineradicable and peculiar attitudes that characterize teachers (as well as students) in such a unique environment. The main character, old-school teacher Straitley, is just lovely and his passion for teaching and culture are contagious. You can not but love the man and wish that you had a teacher like that in your own youth.<br /><br />The finale is also quite good and an apt conclusion to a riveting and well written novel presenting interesting twists and turns. The complex, deep, almost all-consuming relationship between the school and the main characters is beautifully portrayed. St Oswald's School and its peculiar atmosphere with its sounds, smells, and timeless weight of tradition will stay with the reader well after the book is finished. <br /><br />Highly recommended and a well-deserved 4 star rating. </span>

<div id="review_1870079414" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1870079414" />
    <a title="Jeanette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette"><img alt="Jeanette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372095557p2/11869072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1870079414?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette" href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette">Jeanette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1870079414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10974380690661074141">Oh is this a splendid read! I almost gave it 5 stars until just 50 or 70 so pages from the end, when I think Harris jumped the shark a bit. But then I read "Different Class" first, so having given that one the 5 star, I felt this first one just shied behind it. It is 4.5 star if I could give it that rating. <br/><br/>If you have ever taught for a private institution anywhere, this book will cut to your gut with its sharp spears of recognition. Not just in England is there an embodiment like St. O's. Be it</span>
  <span id="freeText10974380690661074141" style="display:none">Oh is this a splendid read! I almost gave it 5 stars until just 50 or 70 so pages from the end, when I think Harris jumped the shark a bit. But then I read "Different Class" first, so having given that one the 5 star, I felt this first one just shied behind it. It is 4.5 star if I could give it that rating. <br /><br />If you have ever taught for a private institution anywhere, this book will cut to your gut with its sharp spears of recognition. Not just in England is there an embodiment like St. O's. Be it for hundreds of years or 120 or a mere 75, tradition matters. As do the "eyes" of the gargoyle in the bell tower room #59. <br /><br />It's a maze of characters and most of them have at least one nickname. The cabals and the choirs of allied voices ever altering and taking juxtaposition. You need to be on your toes. This is no easy or sloppy read possibility. In fact, you may need to backtrack if you happen to catch a hint of what you wanted to "grasp" before that section.<br /><br />The voices are duo narrators. And of course one is always our centurion semester champion. So you also have to focus on who is speaking for that chapter or location. And it helped too, for me, that this was a reread for at least 1/2 of the book. I had this once before, way back in the days when it was a newbie and needed to get it back. Laughingly I thought I could speed through it. NO, this is NOT the book for that possibility. Every nuance counts. And the minutia also makes the mood, the wit, the whole piece living and breathing entire realm of susceptibility cemented within the place and times of St. Oswald's Grammar School for Boys.<br /><br />There are too many passages that are worth quoting to post here. About liars, charm, duplicity, and stolid honesty? And yet their opposites too. Do we ever stay 14 in our cutting likes and dislikes? And the psycho-babble asides and pop references add no little salt and pepper to the campus stew.<br />Or to the town or to the Sunnybakers.<br /><br />Joanne Harris writes well. Now and again there glows a hint of bias- but well forgiven. Because even that is exposed shortly for being there. Like R. Straitley, take his example, miss no glimpse or detail! Highly recommend this book. And after you are finished go on to "Different Class". Don't do it in reverse, as I did. A few characters are in both and I knew who was NOT going to be gone which took away from the planned confusion. Sourgrapes and the League of Nations non-withstanding. <br /><br />Why is it that most educational situations of esteem worth continue to change their room numbers or hall names or building designations? At anywhere from 5 to 10 years, it's always another go around for continued and proper confusions. It isn't only from donor favor, of that I am sure. IMHO, it's new heads using their own "Audere, agere, auferre" powers. Because they can.<br /><br />"To dare, to strive, to conquer." I wonder if the gifter of the fob watch will be returning for a class year #3. If possible or if occurring, I can not wait.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10974380690661074141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_246372222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246372222" />
    <a title="Sonia Gomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1948955-sonia-gomes"><img alt="Sonia Gomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240401639p2/1948955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246372222?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sonia Gomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonia Gomes" href="/user/show/1948955-sonia-gomes">Sonia Gomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1948955-sonia-gomes?shelf=good-but-not-fantastic">good-but-not-fantastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1948955-sonia-gomes?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1948955-sonia-gomes?shelf=kids">kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer246372222&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246372222" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8515939894582847381">How do you feel when you know you are nothing but the porter’s son and will never ever be accepted by any of the boys at St. Oswald’s? <br/>Oh the agony of being overlooked, ignored, despised when you know that you are as good maybe even better than those snoots. <br/>That’s when you transform yourself from Julian Snyde into Julian Pinchbeck, as Julian Pinchbeck you have the run of St. Oswald's, as the porter’s son you have the bunch of keys that allows you to inspect every nook and cranny of St. Oswald, </span>
  <span id="freeText8515939894582847381" style="display:none">How do you feel when you know you are nothing but the porter’s son and will never ever be accepted by any of the boys at St. Oswald’s? <br />Oh the agony of being overlooked, ignored, despised when you know that you are as good maybe even better than those snoots. <br />That’s when you transform yourself from Julian Snyde into Julian Pinchbeck, as Julian Pinchbeck you have the run of St. Oswald's, as the porter’s son you have the bunch of keys that allows you to inspect every nook and cranny of St. Oswald, you know its secrets, its joys and aspirations. As Julian Pinchbeck you can eavesdrop into classes, although never an integral part of St. Oswald, you absorb knowledge like a sponge, you even have a mentor who you respect but also dislike. <br />Although you feel a part of St. Oswald you know that you will never belong and that turns into a violent hatred for St. Oswald. <br />And then along comes Leon the rebel…….You love him with a passion, you will do anything, just about anything to be his friend even when he treats you, your father the porter, and all other people in your social class as something revolting. <br />And then Leon finds out your true identity…….you cannot imagine your life after that, you just cannot imagine…….and then you push him off the roof. <br />You start a new life far away in France but you are never as vulnerable as you were as the porter’s child. You are now educated and know how to look after yourself pretty well, but all along you nurture that awful hatred for St. Oswald’s, you plot and plan your revenge for a decade and then you return to St. Oswald to wreak your terrible revenge from the very inside of St. Oswald, from its very soul you plan to finish St. Oswald. But what new avatar are you planning on?........... <br /> <br />If you look at Julian Snyde/ Julian Pinchbeck's life, it could be ours too. How many times have we suffered slights, people ignoring you, people treating you like a bucket of garbage just because you do not belong to a particular social class, because we are not rich enough, the list is endless....And the harder you try the more you fail.<br /><br />Isn't it better then to be your own poor self? Not to compete? Not to try to be someone or something you just cannot be? So much more comfortable, so much more at ease? Doing what you love and trying not to strive to be someone else. For in such cases the race is endless and the goal never in sight.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8515939894582847381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer674542059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11285856994801119707">Nothing but pure delight -- entertainment at its best, with a few life lessons thrown in, for good measure. <br/><br/>Joanne Harris novels never fail to put me in a good mood, just through the sheer delight of her writing. Sometimes you just need to smile, and be entertained. Sometimes you just need a good game of (psychological) chess to chase away the cobwebs of winter. This delivers on both counts.</span>

<div id="review_78657728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78657728" />
    <a title="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof"><img alt="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268256340p2/1253478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78657728?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)" href="/user/show/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof">The Book Whisperer (aka Boof)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/146034.Gentlemen_and_Players">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=british-authors">british-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=my-most-amazing-books">my-most-amazing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=crime-mystery-thrillers">crime-mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1253478-the-book-whisperer-aka-boof?shelf=uk">uk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78657728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11140244228199069728">What a great book; especially the end where I did NOT see any of those twists coming. It's the sort of book that makes you want to turn to the beginning again to see where you might have picked up clues or see what you missed.<br/><br/>I am a HUGE Joanne Harris fan, my favourites of hers being the "foodie" books and I must admit to being a tad sceptical when I picked this up thinking that maybe she wouldn't do thriller novels quite as well. I was wrong - this lady is no one-trick-pony. From the first page</span>
  <span id="freeText11140244228199069728" style="display:none">What a great book; especially the end where I did NOT see any of those twists coming. It's the sort of book that makes you want to turn to the beginning again to see where you might have picked up clues or see what you missed.<br /><br />I am a HUGE Joanne Harris fan, my favourites of hers being the "foodie" books and I must admit to being a tad sceptical when I picked this up thinking that maybe she wouldn't do thriller novels quite as well. I was wrong - this lady is no one-trick-pony. From the first page you know that there are a murder or two which sets the reader up for the unfolding story ahead. The story is set in a public boys school that is centuries old and has a mighty reputation to uphold and is narrated by two people in turn to keep us guessing. The old school teacher, Mr Straitley, adds some real comic moments too which add warmth to the book. However, whatever you think you know about this book, think again. By three quarters of the way through I guarantee that you will flick back wondering when you could possibly have missed the signs (not once but twice). Mwaaaaahahahahahaha!<br /><br />I highly recommend this book; I had great fun reading it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11140244228199069728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer4088024766122615477">The thing I really like about Joanne Harris (Chocolat, Five Quarters of an Orange, etc.) is that she is not a formula writer. Each of her books is unique and can stand on its own merits. Gentlemen and Players is a bit of a cat and mouse thriller that effectively uses a chess analogy throughout the novel. Lots of twists and turns in this mystery. Many of the characters' names are cleverly used to offer some insights and hints. But don't read too, much about the story beforehand if you want to enj</span>
  <span id="freeText4088024766122615477" style="display:none">The thing I really like about Joanne Harris (Chocolat, Five Quarters of an Orange, etc.) is that she is not a formula writer. Each of her books is unique and can stand on its own merits. Gentlemen and Players is a bit of a cat and mouse thriller that effectively uses a chess analogy throughout the novel. Lots of twists and turns in this mystery. Many of the characters' names are cleverly used to offer some insights and hints. But don't read too, much about the story beforehand if you want to enjoy the full effect of the surprises. </span>

<div id="review_36552866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36552866" />
    <a title="Autumn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/657683-autumn"><img alt="Autumn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239294995p2/657683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36552866?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Autumn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Autumn" href="/user/show/657683-autumn">Autumn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36552866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14686752974132813599">Alright, I'll say right up front that I would have given this book five stars, except that it has more profanity and school-boy crudities than I'm comfortable with in a book. But, (and this might be a bad thing), I'm willing to put up with a little more of that in a really great book. This book is definitely more PG13 than PG.<br/>That being said, it's a great story. It's set in a boys' prep school in England and the story centers around Roy Straitley, a latin professor who has taught there for 33 ye</span>
  <span id="freeText14686752974132813599" style="display:none">Alright, I'll say right up front that I would have given this book five stars, except that it has more profanity and school-boy crudities than I'm comfortable with in a book. But, (and this might be a bad thing), I'm willing to put up with a little more of that in a really great book. This book is definitely more PG13 than PG.<br />That being said, it's a great story. It's set in a boys' prep school in England and the story centers around Roy Straitley, a latin professor who has taught there for 33 years. Chapters are alternately told in his voice, and the voice of an unnamed new professor who plans to "take down" the school. We know from the outset that this new professor is planning murder and mayhem, but we don't know who he is or what he's planning to do. I love Straitley's wry sense of humor and his take on academic life. And the intended murder/mystery aspect is quite gripping. I finished the book sitting on the stairs by the kitchen while my kids ate breakfast one morning.<br /><br />PS - if you don't like profanity, don't look up the meaning to the latin phrases used by the students :) Just so you are forewarned...</span>
  <a data-text-id="14686752974132813599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2860174696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2860174696" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2860174696?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780792739029" href="/book/show/15119.Gentlemen_Players">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2860174696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8258941086238040740"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563479237i/27849469._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Most adults assume that the feelings of adolescence don't count, somehow, and that those searing passions of rage and hate and embarrassment and horror and hopeless, abject love are something your grow out of, something hormonal, a practice run for the Real Thing. It wasn't. At 13 *everything* counts; there are sharp edges on everything, and all of them cut.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>An intriguing storyline and a twisted plot put this one in a whole new category for me. Of course we all know what a </span>
  <span id="freeText8258941086238040740" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563479237i/27849469._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Most adults assume that the feelings of adolescence don't count, somehow, and that those searing passions of rage and hate and embarrassment and horror and hopeless, abject love are something your grow out of, something hormonal, a practice run for the Real Thing. It wasn't. At 13 *everything* counts; there are sharp edges on everything, and all of them cut.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>An intriguing storyline and a twisted plot put this one in a whole new category for me. Of course we all know what a fabulous writer Joanne Harris is, that was never in question. But for the first three quarters of this book, I had to wonder... what is the purpose to all of this. I was even growing a little bored with it. Ha! Little did I know that I was about to be tossed off a cliff. What an ending! It made me see the entire book in a whole new light. Fabulous work. Loved it. And I can't fail to mention the narrator of the audiobook, Steven Pacey, who did a wonderful job. <br>I will look forward to reading many more books by Joanne Harris. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8258941086238040740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=mystery-english">mystery-english</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34892959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9957829106831114183">I honesty think this is Harris' best book. I truly do.<br/><br/>To talk to much about the plot is to give away a bit too many spoilers, and part of the joy of the book is the mystery so, let's not do that. What I love, besides the mystery, is the look at class, gender, and blind love that we can't fully rationalize. There are so many parallels between the central characters and this is a winning aspect of the novel. </span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ?shelf=z_2015-monthly-genre">z_2015-monthly-genre</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222962466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer170494041998888382">A brilliant psychological thriller where the criminal is playing a game of chess with the staff at St Oswald's, a posh all boys’ school, with the aim of bringing down the school by tarnishing its reputation. The main target is an old-fashioned teacher named Quaz (AKA Quasimodo since he resides in the school tower), I loved this character! <br/>The novel alternates chapters from the perpetrator and the old teacher perspective. Harris does a wonderful job in creating a credible psychopath with a grudge</span>
  <span id="freeText170494041998888382" style="display:none">A brilliant psychological thriller where the criminal is playing a game of chess with the staff at St Oswald's, a posh all boys’ school, with the aim of bringing down the school by tarnishing its reputation. The main target is an old-fashioned teacher named Quaz (AKA Quasimodo since he resides in the school tower), I loved this character! <br />The novel alternates chapters from the perpetrator and the old teacher perspective. Harris does a wonderful job in creating a credible psychopath with a grudge. Although I sensed the identity of the perpetrator, it was a very nice twist. The ending felt a little drawn-out, but a very enjoyable read. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47401.Chocolat__Chocolat___1_" title="Chocolat (Chocolat, #1) by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Chocolat</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15096.Five_Quarters_of_the_Orange" title="Five Quarters of the Orange by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Five Quarters of the Orange</a> but stopped reading Harris' novels when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15101.Blackberry_Wine" title="Blackberry Wine by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Blackberry Wine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/321572.Holy_Fools" title="Holy Fools by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Holy Fools</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/103448.Coastliners" title="Coastliners by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Coastliners</a> left me unimpressed. I’m glad I tried <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15102.Gentlemen_and_Players" title="Gentlemen and Players by Joanne Harris" rel="nofollow noopener">Gentlemen and Players</a>, after seeing it mentioned in one GR groups, I’m sure there are other gems of hers for me to discover. A recommended read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="170494041998888382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117838893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3177475720898791866">Wow..what can I say about this book but I was blown away..Its an effort and exercise in vocabulary and patience but well worth it..The surprise twist that comes around page 324 is enough to make this book unforgettable and rare..This is the story of a prestigious all boys day school St. Oswalds and all the characters and secrets it holds are revealed to us by two narrators you love and hate... on one hand you have the loveable old Mr Straitley: a tweed jacket wearing relic of the old academic er</span>
  <span id="freeText3177475720898791866" style="display:none">Wow..what can I say about this book but I was blown away..Its an effort and exercise in vocabulary and patience but well worth it..The surprise twist that comes around page 324 is enough to make this book unforgettable and rare..This is the story of a prestigious all boys day school St. Oswalds and all the characters and secrets it holds are revealed to us by two narrators you love and hate... on one hand you have the loveable old Mr Straitley: a tweed jacket wearing relic of the old academic era when Latin was taught and respected instead of diminished by computer classes..Mr Straitley is cranky, pretentious, stubborn and silly but all in all my favorite teacher in a story as he is so richly drawn. The other narrator tells an alternate tale of St. Oswalds as they constantly feel excluded from the prestige and decorum of the school and so starts the obsessive and intriguing game of revenge and destruction starting with the faculty and unfortunately my Mr Straitley..I was caught up with this book for a week and actually found myself slowing down, rereading and relishing the language and prose of this talented author. She seamlessly intertwines Latin and GRE vocabulary words into a riveting tale with as I stated an amazing twist that made me want to reread the whole story again. I recommend this book to academic staff, aspiring writers, lovers of Latin and a good thrilling read..</span>
  <a data-text-id="3177475720898791866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96693263" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3049657-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264608339p2/3049657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96693263?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/3049657-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3049657-victoria?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3049657-victoria?shelf=lit-fic">lit-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96693263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6696515377886772021">Joanne Harris’ novels have consistently impressed me since first discovering her. She’s a great writer, and I just love the cadence of her prose and the wonderfully realistic characters that she presents in a vivid and rich setting. This more literary mystery of hers is no exception - it’s an enjoyable and entertaining read. The “evil” narrator’s real identity is not impossible to figure out before the end, but it doesn’t detract from the fun in reading it, and adds that wonderful joy of being r</span>
  <span id="freeText6696515377886772021" style="display:none">Joanne Harris’ novels have consistently impressed me since first discovering her. She’s a great writer, and I just love the cadence of her prose and the wonderfully realistic characters that she presents in a vivid and rich setting. This more literary mystery of hers is no exception - it’s an enjoyable and entertaining read. The “evil” narrator’s real identity is not impossible to figure out before the end, but it doesn’t detract from the fun in reading it, and adds that wonderful joy of being right.<br /><br />I also love it when books I read in random order seem to flow together. I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91289.The_Hummingbird_s_Daughter" title="The Hummingbird's Daughter by Luis Alberto Urrea" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hummingbird's Daughter</a> right before this, and had wished for a more smoother way to incorporate foreign language into the fiction. Harris does just that here with interjecting Latin phrases - but unlike Urrea, she includes a very handy glossary in the back of the book. This is one of her best books! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6696515377886772021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060559151" href="/book/show/15108.Gentlemen_and_Players">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer945712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2528641781535857603">May 1st, 2007 (Two weeks before Ava was born)<br/><br/>Not recommended! <br/><br/>I went to Kepler's a week ago and almost came home with four new books. But I instituted an emergency policy on the spot -- only one book purchase allowed -- and I picked this one. It sounded so promising... I love page turners and this was touted as "wickedly funny", literary, and all that good stuff. But my high hopes were dashed! And I gave up after about 120 pages.<br/><br/>In short, two narrators -- one who is supposed to be acerbically wi</span>
  <span id="freeText2528641781535857603" style="display:none">May 1st, 2007 (Two weeks before Ava was born)<br /><br />Not recommended! <br /><br />I went to Kepler's a week ago and almost came home with four new books. But I instituted an emergency policy on the spot -- only one book purchase allowed -- and I picked this one. It sounded so promising... I love page turners and this was touted as "wickedly funny", literary, and all that good stuff. But my high hopes were dashed! And I gave up after about 120 pages.<br /><br />In short, two narrators -- one who is supposed to be acerbically witty and the other who is ominously sinister. But I found neither to be particularly well done. I'm ruined by Arthur Phillips' "The Egyptologist" and Nabokov's "Pale Fire". The unreliable narrators in those novels are finely wrought, hilarious, and clever to boot. This book just felt common.<br /><br />Moving on...<br /><br />--<br /><br />After a comment on my review by a "stranger" on Goodreads, I thought I'd give this book another try. <br /><br />--<br /><br />October 6th, 2010 (Two weeks after David was born)<br /><br />Okay, I'm circling back to review this book more fully, after picking it up again after three years and actually finishing it. First of all, my review from three years ago was totally off-base and mildly embarrassing in retrospect. I don't know what business I had comparing one of the narrators of this novel to the "unreliable narrators" of "Pale Fire" and "The Egyptologist." My guess is that I was actually misusing the phrase "unreliable narrator," because "Gentlemen and Players" has no unreliable narrator.  So, shame on you, Lauren of three years ago!<br /><br />I enjoyed this book after picking it up again. The rough plot is that someone is wreaking havoc at a crusty old-boy prep school in England. That somebody is one of a handful of new teachers, someone who has a history with the school -- harkening back to childhood when they were an outsider, the progeny of the school "porter." It's a sort of whodunit where the reader spends the novel guessing at this individual's identity. I actually knew from the beginning who the "bad guy" was, probably because three years ago when I first attempted to read the book and decided not to finish, I must have skimmed ahead (double shame on me!). But I enjoyed the book nonetheless. It isn't exactly deep, and for more insightful treatments of class at prep schools, I prefer "Prep" by Curtis Sittenfeld and "Old School" by Tobias Wolff. But this was a thriller and a decently-written one. I wouldn't classify it as "literary," because although the writing was steady, the themes weren't particularly insightful or deep.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2528641781535857603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8905713429887701895"><b>Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I really enjoyed this, it's different and quirky despite having dark undertones; the first line reads: 'If there's one thing I've learned in the last fifteen years is that murder is really no big deal.'<br/><br/>Roy Straitley has been the Latin Master at St Oswald's Grammar School for Boys for 33 years. Resistant to change, he's seen as a dinosaur to be humoured but ultimately removed, even though he still commands the respect of the boys and is dedicated to the school.<br/><br/>A new term brings n</span>
  <span id="freeText8905713429887701895" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I really enjoyed this, it's different and quirky despite having dark undertones; the first line reads: 'If there's one thing I've learned in the last fifteen years is that murder is really no big deal.'<br /><br />Roy Straitley has been the Latin Master at St Oswald's Grammar School for Boys for 33 years. Resistant to change, he's seen as a dinosaur to be humoured but ultimately removed, even though he still commands the respect of the boys and is dedicated to the school.<br /><br />A new term brings new teachers, one of whom is full of cunning chaos, and so begins a game of cat and mouse between Roy and his nemesis. Teacher X is a former pupil who bears grudges and is out to destroy the school from within, not in one fell swoop, but piece by delicious piece. Told in alternating chapters by both teachers, the tale also visits the past where as a youngster, Teacher X yearns to fit in with the privileged boys but always feels like an outsider.<br /><br />This is well plotted and well observed. I loved Roy with his cranky dry wit and his weary but defiant views on modern life, and although I guessed X, it didn't detract from a very engaging and unconventional read.</span>

<div id="review_1770057817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1770057817" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9549139-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595701516p2/9549139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770057817?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/9549139-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060559151" href="/book/show/15108.Gentlemen_and_Players">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9549139-kyle?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770057817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16494090665564518195">From what started out as a neat premise quickly devolved into a tedious, meandering puddle of words. I will say this much, I was hooked from the beginning; The plot for revenge by an outcast antihero. Going back and forth in narration between the <b>PAWN</b>, our schemer (with trips back into the past, and present) and the <b>KING</b>, the "Classics" Master, old centurion Mr. Roy Straitley, we find ourselves as readers woven into the murky history of St. Oswald's school for boys, and the lengths some will go </span>
  <span id="freeText16494090665564518195" style="display:none">From what started out as a neat premise quickly devolved into a tedious, meandering puddle of words. I will say this much, I was hooked from the beginning; The plot for revenge by an outcast antihero. Going back and forth in narration between the <b>PAWN</b>, our schemer (with trips back into the past, and present) and the <b>KING</b>, the "Classics" Master, old centurion Mr. Roy Straitley, we find ourselves as readers woven into the murky history of St. Oswald's school for boys, and the lengths some will go to to destroy or preserve it.<br /><br />The darker the subject matter got, the more I found myself enjoying it, but there were too few instances of truly rich and masterful revenge. Most of the time, the book was muddled down by its boring middle portion. The plot to slowly dismantle St. Oswald's by our devious perpetrator is a somewhat remarkable one, but lacks a certain finesse. And the motivations behind it are (to quote an important character) far too "banal." The incentive does not hold enough weight (in my eyes) for the ultimate modus operandi.<br /><br />Also, the twist that occurs during the climax happened to be one of the two routes I theorized it would go. The author does her best to throw you off, and had me thinking a third of the way through the novel that "there's no <i>way</i> that it could be..." But it turns out that it could, and it was. So, there was a sense of lacking any sort of powerful, shocking punch for me by the time the twist was revealed. By then, however, the book was starting to wind down. The ending dragged on and on, and just sort of fizzled out.<br /><br />Could a sequel be in the works? It's certainly a possibility given the circumstances of the ending. I doubt I'd give this story another go, though. All in all, it was a good book. I didn't loathe it, so that's a plus, but I didn't love it, either, and that disappoints me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16494090665564518195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nicole Field" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4641407-nicole-field"><img alt="Nicole Field" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462415079p2/4641407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/662451038?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole Field" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole Field" href="/user/show/4641407-nicole-field">Nicole Field</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback  9780552773379" href="/book/show/4634523-gentlemen-players">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662451038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11262672209659907706">Where do I start with this review?<br/><br/>I've read a number of Joanne Harris' books. Almost all of them.<br/><br/>This one blew all of those books out of the water.<br/><br/>In my experience with her books, I've come to learn that there is a place in the middle where the plot lags, or the characters irritate me, or something just slows down enough for me to put the book down and pick something else up before going back to it.<br/><br/>That point didn't happen in this book. It was fast paced and neat and every character was develope</span>
  <span id="freeText11262672209659907706" style="display:none">Where do I start with this review?<br /><br />I've read a number of Joanne Harris' books. Almost all of them.<br /><br />This one blew all of those books out of the water.<br /><br />In my experience with her books, I've come to learn that there is a place in the middle where the plot lags, or the characters irritate me, or something just slows down enough for me to put the book down and pick something else up before going back to it.<br /><br />That point didn't happen in this book. It was fast paced and neat and every character was developed to a point where I felt satisfied and wanted to hear more of them.<br /><br />And then there were the twists! Impossible to say any more about them without spoiling, really, but I'll tell you that there were 20 pages in there that just one thing after the other had me gasping and shaking the book in front of me at the same time as being unable to pull my eyes from it. <br /><br />Man, what a ride. <br /><br />If there was a higher star rating to give, I would give it. There was absolutely nothing wrong with this book, it was seamless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11262672209659907706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1394928-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405367803p2/1394928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203386148?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1394928-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=xx-2011-xx">xx-2011-xx</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203386148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5627087658109584231">4-4.25 stars. A solid, good read! Fantastic, believable characters, excellent writing. It loses a bit because I hated the villain TOO much. The audio performance is amazing. Better than the book. If you're looking for a cat-and-mouse suspense read, this is it. The older Latin teacher - I will never forget him. What a three-dimensional, awesome man I would love to meet. Any teacher I think would especially appreciate this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
